<Author>Modern_Phrenologist
<Content>good room in central location The hotel must have begun life as something else because the lobby appears to have been a bar at one time. Buffet breakfast (not included in our room rate) is served in the bar. It is adequate for the price with the usual cold meats and cheeses, breads and even a hot plate with eggs, sausage and bacon.Our room (103) was a delux room. It was large, very clean and quiet even though there was quite a bit of Christmas noise in the street until about 23.00 each night. There was an elevator to the room but you must walk up 5 or 6 steps to reach it. The desk clerk carried our bags up the stairs to the elevator so that was not a problem. People with mobility issues might want to look elsewhere.The location, as others have said, is excellent. It is a short block from the Plaza Mayor and a few hundred yards from the Puerta del Sol. It is surrounded by restaurants, bars and other places to have a meal or a snack. Most museums and other places of interest are within walking distance within 15 to 30 minutes. The metro is a five minute walk away.Although services are limited, it met all our needs and I would certainly return on our next trip to Madird.

<Author>nbologne
<Content>Liked everything but the noise We stayed for 3 days in September 2007.Location: Excellent. Within walking distance to the main points of interest (e.g., sights, restaurants, shopping). Close to public transportation.Room: We had a corner room on one of the upper floors. Although the room was clean and nicely decorated, I did not like having a corner room. We were right above the bus station and the buses running all night and all day drove me crazy. If you are a light sleeper like me you will find this annoying. The doors for the windows were also broken so we had a hard time closing them (and no one wants to be exposed to the public in their hotel room while changing, in their sleep wear, etc.) I would ask for a room away from the bus stop. However we did have a large view of the plaza, and all the action outside, so maybe for some this would be okay. Front Desk: Very friendly and helpful. Overall: We had a good stay. Would stay here again but away from the bus stop.

<Author>fpekanto
<Content>Great central location! Hotel Plaza Mayor is really central to everything that we wanted to see. Very close to Atocha train station, to Plaza Mayor, Royal Palace and the Big 3 Museums. We booked through Venere.com based on the reviews on tripadvisor. What we didn't realise was between the reception and the elevator, there were a number of stairs along the way, which makes it quite difficult with our luggages. But the reception did offer help, so that was appreciated. The room that we got was not facing the street so it was pretty quiet, standard size (not big, but not cramped either) and the bathroom was clean. Wireless internet is free but you need to pay if you don't have your laptop with you. Brekky and the use of safety box is not included. Otherwise, this hotel serves the purpose, great location, helpful reception staff who helped with directions, maps and reservations. It has a homey feel to it, as there is living room area in front of our room with books on the shelves (left by previous guests, I assume. Great idea!).

<Author>Maggie1001
<Content>Great Choice for Madrid Break I just returned from a 4 night break in Madrid and was impressed with Hotel Plaza Mayor. We did book the suite on the 6th floor for the extra space but I also saw the superior double room on the 5th floor which was quite spacious for European standards. As the suite is the only room on the 6th floor, we didn't have any problems with noise from other residents and had peaceful sleep each night. The location of the hotel is really central and very convenient for bars, cafes, shopping and sightseeing. We didn't have the breakfast in the hotel as preferred to sample the local cafes and there is plenty of options to choose from. Each room has individual air con / heat which was needed as it was a chilly 5/6 degrees during our stay in Madrid. Staff were pleasant and helpful throughout.I would recommend this hotel to any class of traveller but definitely think the superior rooms on 5th floor or suite is the best option as they aren't too pricey for such a central hotel and worth that little extra cost for comfort.

<Author>genieCanada
<Content>#9 on Trip Advisor list of Madrid hotels? Must be a joke! Since my overall experience was very negative, I will list positives first:- Clean- Nice renovated bathroom (marble, good water pressure)- Friendly and helpful front desk staff- Location (next to plaza Mayor, 2 mins walk to Puerta del Sol)The hotel itself and the room are clearly nothing more than a 2* -- chintzy furniture, spartan bed, skinny pillows, ratty blanket, no mini fridge, pay extra for safe.So how come I rated it a 1* instead of 2+? Counting down in order:3) First floor window faced into an inner courtside. That mean no external noise on the one hand, but on the other hand created an impression of being entombed at the bottom of a narrow well. It might as well have been made into a wall instead of a window. Dingy room paint  furniture inside + absence of natural light (let alone a decent view) outside meant for a depressing overall feeling. Best advice is just sleep and get out.2) Price: Paying 95 euros a night for this hotel is a ripioff. There are got to be tons of better hotels for same money or same hotels for less money.3) A must for a hotel is to allow a good night sleep. However the room acoustics would be worthy of a fine concert hall. Late night revelers coming back to the hotel? Will keep you up. Somebody talking at normal volume? You will hear. Turning on a tap or a shower in a neighboring room? Sounds like Niagara next door. No I am not kidding and I am not an extremely light sleeper. However 3 out of 4 nights we were woken up and kept up until the noise stopped.For the heck of it after the first depressing night we stopped by Hotel Regente near by and asked to see their room (being made up). Both hotel  room are much nicer looking (hotel is listed as 3*), they had vacancy...and the cost was only 80 euros. The only reason we didn't switch was because Hotel Mayor held us hostage (i.e. would have meant paying 1 night penalty for cancellation).In short, unless you are truly desperate (last minute) or can get an amazing rate, look elsewhere. But if you ignore my advice and go by many more people who loved this hotel can't all be wrong, my feelings won't be hurt :-)

<Author>SpikeDaisy
<Content>A Gem We recently stayed here four nights and really enjoyed our stay. The best aspect of this hotel is its location. It is centrally located in Madrid and just a short walk to most major sites. Only about a 10 minute walk to the train station which is very handy for side trips to Toledo, El Escorial, etc. The staff was very helpful and friendly. We'd like to give a shout-out to Dominique, who was particularly helpful. The rooms are clean and tastefully decorated. Our room was actually a little larger than what we have come to expect from most European hotels. While you're in Madrid make sure to frequent the local tapa bars. We really enjoyed Casa Toni (awesome fried eggplant), Oreja de Oro (sauteed miniature green peppers, my fave), and La Casa del Abuelo (anything with shrimp is great). Also make sure to try churros con chocolate at Chocolateria San Gines, near Puerta del Sol. Also a few restaurants we enjoyed were La Gloria de Montera Restaurante and La Paella Real Restaurante.

<Author>TapasFibe
<Content>Great value, perfect position Booked this hotel after hours of research on t'internet, finally discovering Tripadvisor.com and going with their recommendation! Nicely priced hotel, 275 euros for three nights over Bank Holiday (inc. tax), extremely clean and smart. Good customer care, even tho a non-working room safe couldn't be fixed and no reasonable alternative available. Best thing about this hotel is the location. Right next to Plaza Mayor and a spit away from many other must see sights. Having read reviews of other hotels in Madrid it seems that this is a popular complaint but... Take ear plugs with you for night time! There's something about the construction of the building which means that all and any noise from other guests, no matter how considerate or reasonable they're being, reverberates around the rooms. Every foot fall, tap being turned on, shower being run WILL disturb you. Very odd. My top tips: Don't bother with the hotel buffet breakfast. Get up. Get out and sample one of the many little bars which do kick-you-in-the-arse wake up coffee, croissants and toast. DO NOT go to Plaza Mayor on your first night, a little bit tired and weary, sit down at one of the tables in the Plaza corner and say 'Si' to any waiter who comes up and says I will bring you tapas. Tonight you eat like Spaniards, yes? Because if you do, then like us (uninitiated in the ways of tapas, virgin Madrid types) you will be brought six plates of varying dead sea creatures, including tentacles, all of which I'm sure were really delicious if that's your thing. But then, and most importantly, you will be charged... 97.50 euros!!!! (That's 拢78!!) Budget blown, feeling a bit ripped off, we were much more cautious the rest of the weekend and found excellent restaurants and tapas bars everywhere for very reasonable prices. Hey, you live and learn!DO use the Metro. Cheap and straight forward. And finally, DO as the Madrinelos do and wander slowly, admiring the awesome statues, historic buildings and creaky old bars. Stopping every 45 minutes or so for 'refreshments'. My kind of weekend...

<Author>mal_bath
<Content>Ideal Location and Great Value A small, apparently family-owned hotel located just a few steps from Plaza Mayor. Ideally located for all major attractions in Madrid. The staff are very friendly and helpful, even loaning us a Nokia phone charger and checking the location of a restaurant that another Tripadvisor traveller had recommended.We booked directly with the hotel, through its website, having seen a recommendation in the Saturday Travel section of The Daily Telegraph in July 2008. Initially, we requested a corner room (as others had suggested) at 95 Euros per night, but enquired about the suite. The hotel replied within 12 hours, confirming its availability. At 120 Euros, we thought it very good value, considering its size (basically, in the hotel attic/loft) and facilities (a super outside terrace - 6 floor up and with views over the Madrid rooftops!). The only slight downsides were a bed that began to feel a little hard after 4 nights (it is a firm mattress onto a solid divan) and some small amount of noise that permeated the roof (although these were police sirens, and so very loud). You also need to lug bags up the final short flight of steps from the 5th floor, as the lift stops there, so it's worth remembering for those who may struggle. My wife was not so impressed with the lack of a mirror in the room, although there is one with ample lighting in the bathroom. The TV has a variety of European channels, plus CNN and Eurosport. There was also (what appeared to be) a DVD player, though we didn't use it.We visited at an exceptionally hot time (late 30s Celsius), but the room AirCon worked well and the curtains and roof blinds (for the 3 Velux windows) kept out the heat and light. Others have criticised the bathroom for 'only' having one sink! However, we found this to be ample, as it is large and square. The shower could easily accommodate two people, and whilst it didn't seem to drain especially well during use, it never overflowed. Water pressure was fine and supplies of soap and towels plentiful. The room was always kept very clean and laundry changed regularly. Decor is pleasant - stylist, yet subtle. The impression was one of a staff who took pride in the hotel, as there were even pot plants on the terrace.Overall, a great room and a lovely small hotel. We would not have changed it.We took breakfast on the first morning. At 7.50 Euros per person, it is fine if you're hungry/thirsty, as you can help yourselves to the usual selection of fruit, juice, coffee, cheese, bread, croissants, etc. We tried other places for breakfast, too. These were cheaper, but only because you pay per item. For example, juice, coffee and a slice of toast at the cafe diagonally across the small square in front of the hotel cost us around 5 Euros each. As an alternative, we bought some fruit, juice, etc. and breakfasted on the terrace, before grabbing a coffee later.Overall, we'd definitely recommend this hotel. Although it has no pool, restaurant (for lunch/dinner), gym, etc. its superb location and overall value make it hard to beat. We would be very happy to return.From the Airport, the Metro will take you to Sol, from which it's a 5-10 min walk. We were warned about pickpockets, so be careful, though we never encountered any problems and noticed a good police presence on the streets. Sol is very busy, and an obvious target area. Metro lines are numbered and colour-coded, so it's easy to travel around. Tickets from (or to) the Airport cost 2 Euros each (a higher price than travelling around within the city), but you can buy a ticket for 10 trips and use that between 2 or more people once you're travelling around in central Madrid. Ticket machines take coins and notes, but we never managed to get the credit card ones to accept out UK cards. They also have an option for English text, which is helpful.Credit cards are widely accepted, but be aware that they sometimes ask for photo ID. We encountered a grumpy woman at the Prado who refused to accept a card without one. This requirement is not universally applied, and so can catch you out. We visited Toledo one day (9 Euros per person each way) and had no trouble buying the ticket at Madrid, but had to show ID at Toledo. The fast train leaves from Platform 8 (from recollection) and takes 30 mins. You need to buy a ticket at each end.We visited the usual sites, but one worth considering is Plaza de la Villa (the old Town Hall), just off C/Mayor at the Palacio Real end, which provides free guided tours in English on a Monday evening only (at 17:00, from recollection). This is worth visiting for the short tour of an old and interesting building, although some of the interiors may change once the Mayor's offices relocates to alternative accommodation in Madrid.We would suggest a (free) visit to the gardens of the Palacio Real, which are located behind and below the Palace. The ONLY entrance and exit is a small gate off Paseo de la Virgen de Puerto, near to the Principe Rio Metro end. We discovered this on our final morning, sadly too late to spend too much time there or to take a picnic. There are lovely walks, tame birds, fountains and a small pond with terrapins and ducklings. We thought it much nicer than the Parque de el Retiro, as the gardens are more carefully tended and therefore closer to what we would expect to see in a similar grand house/palace garden here in the UK. Definitely worth a visit for a 'green' break from the city.Restaurants:We tried El Escaldon for Tapas (non-smoking upstairs) on C/Cava Baja, but there are lots of others on the same street - just a 5 min walk from Plaza Mayor. Tapas for 2, with desert, Sangria/water/coffee came to around 62 Euros. Service was very pleasant and the food good.We also followed the recommendations posted by other travellers and dined at La Gloria Montera (twice!) on C/Caballero de Gracia (just down from Gran Via Metro) and La Finca de Susana on C/Ariaban (close to Sevilla Metro). Both were superb, but also very popular with the Spanish. They are both non-smoking, offer a variety of food and open around 20:30. Highly recommended! We could not understand why people would choose Macdonald's over restaurants such as these which offer superb food and service, in lovely surroundings at a very good price. One thing that we did notice is that neither place applied the usual rip-off prices for wine that we have to put up with in the UK. In fact, the wine was very pleasant and inexpensive - a quite reasonable bottle being less than 10 Euros. Our meal for 2 (3 courses with wine/water) came to around 50 Euros. Excellent value!All three restaurants take credit cards and have English-speaking staff.We also used Cerveceria 100 Montaditos, next to the Opera House (close to Opera Metro) for lunch. They do small rolls with 100 different fillings, are cheap and great for lunch. 6 rolls is ample for 2 people. With 2 juices/waters/coffees, our bill was 15 Euros. We heard that this place was being recommended by tour guides. The staff were friendly, but spoke mainly Spanish.The nearest Tourist Information is on Plaza Mayor.We hope that you find this information helpful in planning your visit to Madrid and that you enjoy the city as much as we did!

<Author>zolo
<Content>A Quintiessential Small European Hotel Like others, when travelling to Europe, I have a picture of a hotel in my head. You know the type; often described as 'romantic' or 'quaint' . Four to six stories high. Small, but not too small. Not on a big thoroughfare, but not impossible to find either. Near the sites in a neighbourhood oozing the local culture. Full of old world charm but not lacking in the modern amenity category. A room that when you wake-up you know immediately you are in Europe. Well, this hotel fufilled my fantasy on every level! Start with the location, overlooking the Plaza Santa Cruz and only 150 meters from the Plaza Mayor, perhaps Madrid's classiest destination. The building is mature, but the hotel is only 10 years old. It is tastefully decorated throughout and well engineered. Let me focus on the wonderfull windows, over two meters high that allow plenty of light and fresh air in. Close the shutters and it becomes as dark as you need and the glass window is well constructed so that it is remarkable how much outside noise it mutes. I even liked the breakfast (maligned by other reviewers). At 7 euros it comes hassle-free and is fresh and varied so that you are bound to find something you like. At night, the desk clerk will often let you use the internet for free. Here are some local tips. The city's best tourist information office is in the Plaza Mayor. From it, you can catch some real cheap, English speaking, walking tours (Madrid must be the most easily walkable great city). The Calle de la Bolsa is a small, pedestrian friendly street that starts just outside of the hotel and easily links with the Plaza Santa Ana and eventually the Paseo del Prado.

<Author>TrickyRick
<Content>As good as promised I had planned our trip to Spain for the past year and the consensus opinion amongst all of the guidebooks I regularly use (Rick Steves, Frommer's and Lonely Planet) about where to stay in Madrid was the Hotel Plaza Mayor so I never really considered any other place. I have to say that they were all right on the money. We stayed in Madrid for four nights and could tell right off the bat that our stay was going to be enjoyable. The location couldn't be beat - a stone's throw from the Plaza and a five minute walk from the Puerta del Sol. And although it was so centrally located the outside noise from the street was not too bad at all and keep in mind that our first night there was the start of the San Isidro Festival! The room size was fairly large by my knowledge of European standards and the bathroom was also of a good size. We ate breakfast at the hotel each morning and it was excellent - a selection of hams and sausages as well as bread and fruit, etc. Everyone at the hotel was extremely friendly and helpful and did their best to make our stay as enjoyable as possible. And the kicker is - the rates (even factoring in the lousy dollar/euro exchange rate) were extremely reasonable. To sum up, I would wholeheartedly recommend the Hotel Plaza Mayor to anyone visiting Madrid.

<Author>combattant
<Content>Central, clean hotel with helpful staff. Just stayed at the Plaza Mayor based on therecommendations found here. We found the place central - Plaza Mayor a stones throw away, The Prado and The Reina Sofia 10 - 15 mins down c/Atocha if you can resist stopping at the fab bakers and cafes as you walk down the hill and Puerta del Sol 5 mins. The room was clean and the staff helpful - on our final day the receptionist told us to go and see the Changing of the Guard at the Royal Palace (10 minutes walk) - we were not aware it was on as it only takes place every 1st Wednesday of the month from September to June. Some good restaurants not very far away are 'La Finca de Susana' on c/Arlaban and a bit closer 'Ginger' on Plaza del Angel - both look upmarket but have reasonably priced interesting menus and definitely worth a visit for their menu del dia at lunch (siesta obligatory afterwards!) or dining a la carte in the evening. Moore's Irish Pub just off the north side of Plaza Mayor is worth a visit for a refreshing pint of the black stuff, especially if you are a sad Man Utd fan who cannot miss a match even whilst having a jolly in Madrid. You can take the lad out of Manchester but you cannot take Manchester out of the lad! Looking for a more authentic Castllian bar - try Naturbier on Plaza Santa Ana with an interesting variety of sausages on the menu as well as their microbrewed beer. Unfortunately one sight in Madrid that definitely did not impress was the Bernabeu - but you may suspect we were slightly biased!

<Author>needdm
<Content>Very nice small hotel Centrally situated. I stayed at the hotel over the Easter Weekend for 4 nights with my family, and had two rooms(one superior twin, and one triple), the rooms were very similiar, and although fairly small were sufficient for our needs. Rooms had a flat screen tv with access to around 10 TV channels, although only CNN was in English. Bathrooms were ok with a bath and shower, although the bath was fairly small.We requested quiet rooms, which were on the first floor towards the back of the hotel, and were not disturbed at all by noise. The hotel was very clean, and the staff were very friendly. There is a small breakfast area near reception and the breakfasts on offer seemed very good, however as the breakfast was not included in the price we choose to eat out. The Museo de Jarbon was the best place we found for breakfast, but there are lots of other alternatives. The hotel is well situated, about 100 yards from Plaza Mayor, and close to the Sol Metro station. The Hotel was easy to get to from the airport by metro, although you do have to change trains at least twice due to the layout of the metro system. The royal palace, and the main musuems can be walked to within 15 minutes. I should mention two wonderful restaurants about 5 to 10 minutes walk away from the hotel (La Finca de Susana on C/Ariabain, and La Gloria de Montera on C/Caballero de Gracia) which I would highly recommend. Neither can be booked, so it is worth getting there 10 minutes before they open at 8.30pm. There was a long queue of locals at both restaurants, which is always a good sign. The food was wonderful with a varied menu, and very reasonable (鈧?00 for 5) It is also worth going to a show at Las Carboneras if you are interested in getting a taste of flamenco dancing. This is only 5 minutes from the hotel across Plaza Mayor..

<Author>irishmm
<Content>clean, comfortable, affordable Traveling to Madrid as a solo female, I felt safe in this very clean and well-located hotel (just steps from the Plaza del Sol and the Plaza Mayor). From my initial experience booking on the Internet, to checking in and out, I found the employees of the Hotel Plaza Mayor to be muy amable...very kind and helpful. English spoken here, though all tolerated my sincere attempts to speak Spanish. I stayed in room 504, a small room with a twin bed, for 60 euros per night. The bathroom (toilet, sink, shower) was spotless, and yes, small again. But who spends much time in their room in Madrid? I was very happy with the room, for the price. The room also had a safe (1.2 Euros per day), a TV, and a desk. Pequeno, si, but functional. My room overlooked a small, charming Plaza, which was busy for much of the day and into the night, but on the 5th floor, I heard very little with windows closed. No sounds from other rooms either, though the hotel was almost full during the time I was there.The Hotel offers breakfast for an additional fee. I recommend trying the small cafe directly across the plaza (to the left) in front of the Hotel, for a cafe con leche and pastry (2.10 Euros).Also - Consider having dinner with steak (solomillo) at Casa Paco's, a few minutes' walk from the Hotel (Puerta Cerrada 11, just off the Plaza Mayor), with salad and Valdepenas red wine. This will set you back a few Euros, but worth every penny. Enjoy.

<Author>MPortland
<Content>Nice hotel near Plaza Mayor This hotel was nice, with a charming facade and interior. Our room was clean and air conditioned; we stayed on an upper front corner, room 203. Our room was large and had all the amenities, including a desk. The best thing was that it was well insulated from the pollution and noise of this district, yet the windows were quite large so the room had very good light. The bathroom was all tile with a tub/shower. The elevator was handy, although there are stairs before you get there. The staff was friendly, bilingual, professional, and available 24 hours. I'd skip the breakfast; it is overpriced and not very interesting. Instead try the litte Peter Pan coffee shop down the street. We would definitely stay here again.

<Author>Mytravelreview68
<Content>Small hotel, small rooms. Good location The hotel is in the center of Madrid so it is far from the airport.If you are going for sightseeing, it s a very good location. It is not for business trips. The rooms are very small. You can here everything coughs, sneezing conversations ..everything. If you are over say 6ft you wouldn t fit in the beds. The staff is nice. The hotel is basically clean. Bathrooms are way small. So bottom line for the 70 or 80 euros you can get any hotel you want just by booking through the airline. Anyone who gives this a 5 or says it s a gem must have never traveled before. If you re not in the hotel all day it may work. If you plan to be in the room say two hours during the day and 6-7 hours to sleep it s going to be way uncomfortable. There are local hotel chains which may not be as nice on the outside, but are way more comfortable inside and have much bigger rooms and higher ceilings. Bottom line, a good hotel, not the best, not the worst, a 3 at best. Best is location if you re on vacation, worst is small rooms, 4 x 4 ft bathrooms, small beds and paper thin walls. Lobby smells awful during breakfast hour.All in all, its doable for folks on vacation

<Author>hedylarue
<Content>Great hotel in a prime location I was very happy with my decision to stay at the Plaza Mayor during my visit to Madrid.I stayed in a superior double room which are apparently only on the first floor. I was nervous that there would be a lot of street noise, but the first floor of the hotel is actually off the street and reallymore like a second floor. The walls are thin and if there is a lot of noise inside or outside you will hear it but I didn't have a problem.The other guests were quiet and the hotel is not located on a super busy street so the sounds outside were not a problem. I was expecting the room to be tiny, but I actually thought it was a good size by European standards. Even the bathroom was a decent size...there is an actual tub and not just a stand up shower. The water pressure and temperature of the hot water was great and that can be rare! The subway, shopping areas and many restaurants are very close by.Breakfast is extra: 7 Euros/person. I never tried it. I did go to the famous Chocolateria San Gines a couple of blocks away for their chocolat con churros and that was great. Also close by is Botin, the oldest restaurant in the world!

<Author>A_Fellow_Traveler
<Content>Good--but compare to the Europa Hotel Plaza Mayor IS a very close walk to one of the city's prime tourist attractions: the Plaza itself. My son and I found it to be clean, safe and convenient. The showers were extraordinarily small, however. For the same price (actually at bit less I think, because tax was included), we also stayed at the Hotel Europa one night. That place had larger rooms and showers, and was NO less centrally located (right by the Plaze del Sol--a very convenient metro stop.) The Europa also had a restaurant right off the lobby, and free internet (which Plaza Mayor did not). So while they both represent good values for the money, I would recommend Europa over this place.

<Author>Clarts
<Content>A good choice In. contrast to the previous review I found the staff very friendly and helpful and all spoke good English. One in particular spent a long time translating a menu for us. The hotel is in an excellent position and how quiet the rooms are will depend on if you have one by the street or inside. We had one inside which was very quiet but lacked a little natural light. The windows are tall but face a small courtyard with rooms above. If you want ventilation you will have to stand on a chair to open the top hung window although there is air conditioning. The rooms were clean but basic, i.e laminate floors instead of carpet but better clean laminate than stained carpet. The bathroom was fine but beware of sudden changes in water temperature when using the shower, also our friends in another room had to run the water for a while to get it hot.The breakfast consisted of cereals, toast,bread,fruit, juices, pastries , bacon and scrambled eggs. My friends and I thought it was ample and good value. There are safes in the rooms to hire for 1.5 euros a day. All things considered I think for a 2 star hotel in that location it was a good choice. You could easily spend a lot more and get a lot less for it. I was more than happy with our stay and think the hotel deserves the positive reviews it gets from the majority of posters.

<Content>Great Hotel Just returned from a 4 night stay at the Plaza Mayor. The hotel was excellent and extremely good value for money. We booked directly through the hotels website after being recommended in 3 travel books and the reviews on here. We were not let down. The room was spacious and had plenty of room for everything. There was a flat wide screen tv on the wall, and a safe could be rented for 鈧?.20 a night. Bathroom was of adequate size with an excellent shower.The lights in the hallway do have to be switched on - we were at the end of the very long corridor but this was never a problem as the switches glow. Our room looked out onto one of the side streets, and outside noise was not a problem. We were however woken by what must've been a noisy pipe system!Location was fantastic - everything was so close, and could not have asked for more. 2 mins to the Plaza Mayor and about 5 mins from Sol Station. The staff were very nice and friendly and helpful when we wanted train times. There is also somewhere where you can leave your luggage after check out.I would definitly recommend the hotel and would stay here again.

<Author>Travel_Chick5
<Content>A Very Nice Place to Stay I traveled solo to Madrid, Barcelona, and Toledo at the end of May, and I stayed in four different hotels. Out of all of them, Hotel Plaza Mayor in Madrid was one of the best. I stayed there for two nights at the very end of my trip and was very pleased overall. This hotel was the most expensive of the four (though still very affordable) but it was worth every cent. LOCATION: As the name suggests, the hotel is located very close to the Plaza Mayor, but it鈥檚 far enough away so that you can鈥檛 really hear the noise from the Plaza itself. I was really happy with the location, as Plaza Mayor ended up being my favorite place to sit and people-watch. The hotel is only a few blocks from the Puerta Sol metro stop, which is great if you鈥檙e taking the metro to the airport. It鈥檚 also very easy to find if you鈥檙e arriving from the Atocha train station: once you exit the train station, you just stay on the same street all the way to the hotel (Be aware, however that it鈥檚 a slightly uphill walk from the train station to the hotel. If you have luggage, you might want to just hop in a cab).HOTEL: The hotel had a medium sized (rather quiet and peaceful) lobby that also served as a breakfast room. I didn鈥檛 have breakfast at the hotel, mainly because I wanted to sleep in. There is one computer in the lobby with Internet access, but I think they charge for the use of it. It was almost always in use. The connection is very slow apparently, so I just used the Internet caf茅 four blocks away. I had to go up a flight or two of stairs, then down two long hallways to get to my room. The hallways had lovely little couches and shelves that were simply overflowing with books 鈥?very nice if you wanted to relax, read, and take a short rest. One thing to know about the hotel: the lights in the hallways go off at night. It caught me by surprise when I walked out of my room on the first night, and it was pitch black - but my eyes quickly adjusted. I noticed that they do this in several hotels in Spain. Just know where the light switches are in the hallway and you鈥檒l be fine. STAFF: I encountered several different front desk clerks during my stay. For me, the staff at a hotel can make or break an experience and can determine whether or not I will stay there again. Almost all of the staff members at Hotel Plaza Mayor were very professional and friendly, and all of them spoke English. The night shift clerk spoke the least English, but he was very sweet and helpful when I attempted to speak Spanish. In the afternoon, a young man and an older woman were working at the front desk 鈥?they were amazing! The young man helped me plan my Metro route to the airport, drew maps, and downloaded information on the computer. And through it all, he was wonderfully patient and good-humored. The older woman who was working at the same time was also quite nice and had extremely helpful suggestions. I do have to add that at one point in the afternoon, there was a younger college-aged woman 鈥渨orking鈥?at the front desk who was obviously way too busy flirting with any men who happened to walk by to do her job: she literally ignored every single female guest who came to the front desk to ask for help (I watched this go on for a good 30 minutes). It would have been downright comical if it hadn鈥檛 been so blatantly rude. If I had dealt only with her, I wouldn鈥檛 have stayed there again - no matter how nice the hotel itself was. However, the other staff members were absolutely phenomenal, and my experiences with them more than made up for her behavior. Overall, everyone was very professional and the service was fantastic, so I would definitely stay there again.ROOM: I stayed in a double room with two single beds. It was nice to have the extra space of a double room for a change. Since I was packing for my return trip home, I used the second twin bed to lay out all my stuff and get organized. With regard to sleeping, the bed was very comfortable, with nice crisp sheets (Note: I鈥檓 5鈥?鈥漚nd 125 pounds, and the twin bed felt a bit too small for me鈥?so if you鈥檙e bigger than that, and you decide stay there, you might want to request a double bed). I also really liked the layout of the room. It had a huge sliding glass door, and there was a little patio outside. The sunlight filtered in softly, creating a very peaceful ambience. What else...I made good use of the safe, which I believe they charged for by the day. You have to pick up a key card and program your own code. Last of all: the shower was just wonderful.OVERALL: I liked this hotel the best because of the overall impression it left me with. The entire place was immaculate and modern, but at the same time, it was restful and welcoming. At the end of a two-week trip full of hustle and bustle, it felt like a quiet oasis where I could get my bearings and feel fully rested before the long flight home. I would definitely return. I can honestly say that it was the nicest place that I stayed at in Spain. LAST TIP: It鈥檚 cheaper if you book directly with the hotel via fax or email.

You can walk the streets and get a good feeling for several surrounding neighborhoods, complete with tapas and sites.We arrived very early (around 9am), and they had our room ready for us in about 15 minutes. They've got wireless access and low-fee internet access in the main lobby. Our room was 75 Euros a night, with a nice view of the Madrid rooftops from the 5th floor and a powerful little air conditioner that kept the room nice and cool, even in July. The rooms are small, but clean, and there's an elevator to get you and your luggage to the upper floors.The hotel is in an urban environment, and when we were checking out a pickpocket came in and tried to steal wallets from both my husband and a woman at the internet station, but the hotel staff and other customers were very vigilent and assertively drove him off, so disaster was averted! All part of the hotel's great location in a major city center....We felt very well cared for.

<Author>B40
<Content>Little Gem! I booked the Hotel Plaza Mayor after reading other reviews on Trip Advisor and we were not disappointed!I agree that it is in a great location and excellent value for money. The hotel was clean and the staff friendly  helpful.We stayed in a superior twin room, which was perfect for our short stay. It wasn't the biggest of rooms, however it was no smaller than some of the other hotels I have stayed in when in various european cities. The beds were comfortable and the room was well equipped.I liked the way the corridors were furnished; our floor also had a book exchange. The corridor had a carpet runner along the centre of the wooden flooring - great for cutting down the noise of footsteps from other guests returning late at night.When arriving in Madrid we took the metro from the airport to the centre of the city. The metro is fast, efficient and easy to use. We took Line 8 (pink line) to Colombia (4 stops), then changed to Line 9 (purple line) for Principe de Vergara (5 stops), then finally took Line 2 (red line) to Sol (4 stops). The whole journey cost just 2 euros. When exiting the metro you need to take the exit for Calle Mayor and follow the signs to Plaza Mayor. Once on the Plaza, head in the same direction as Felipe III's horse and you will see the sign of the hotel through one of the arches in the right corner.We had a great time in Madrid and I would like to go back.........and yes, I would definately stay in the Hotel Plaza Mayor!

<Author>TracyPit
<Content>Can't beat location and price It's taken me some time to write this review, so forgive me. My husband and I stayed here in October 2006.PROS:LOCATION and PRICE. Can't be beat. You walk out your door and you are in the Plaza Mayor. Taxis are always available right outside of the hotel if needed, but you are centrally located to most everything.CONS:Tiny, tiny room. Could barely fit me, my husband (who is rather tall) and our luggage. The shower stall was pretty claustrophobia-inducing... kind of tight in there when trying to wash my hair, etc. Also, the hallway was really, really dark which we found kind of bizarre at first. I think it's on a sensor but it would take a little time to go on. A bit scary when first exiting the elevator. Lastly, we almost did not get to see the flamenco show that we wanted and it was the last night of our trip. The receptionist assured us that they made us a reservation, but when we got to the venue, we were not on the list. Luckily, there was one slot available as long as we weren't going to eat dinner. We weren't so we got lucky, but that was a bit disappointing. Oh, and though I am a New Yorker, I would have to say that Madrid never sleeps! The party went on all night long and so it was rather loud. The voices seemed to reverberate through the square. Bring earplugs if you get bothered by that.Overall, I would recommend this hotel because of its great location/price. Just don't plan on spending too much time in the room.

<Author>uribes
<Content>Great Hotel - Great Location We stayed at this hotel for 4 nights during our trip to Spain last May. Could not have made a better choice. The hotel is very clean and the location is excellent. You can walk to all the important places in less than 10 minutes. The subway station is also very close. The Plaza Mayor and Plaza del Sol are a few blocks away. We asked for a room in the top floor with a balcony and a view to the street, could not have asked for more. It was just great. <Content>Great Location, Great Price A recent comment was that there was nothing special about this hotel, and they are right - it is just a hotel. However, it is only a 3 minute walk from the Metro, and within walking distance to the major attractions in Madrid. The hotel is very clean, and it is one of the cheapest hotels you can book in Madrid. This is what makes it a great deal, even if there is nothing special otherwise to be said. We also found the rooms sizes vary greatly. The couple we traveled with had a room twice the size of ours (paid the same price) although we had a window view to the city, and they did not. The breakfast in the morning was also very good, with plenty of options, breads, fruits, juices, cereals, etc. I would not hesistate to stay here the next time I am in Madrid.

<Author>Jdian
<Content>Tripadvisor does it again! Just got back from a three night stay at the Plaza Mayor and the hotel was every bit as good as the vast majority of the reviews on Tripadvisor suggested. Excellent location, friendly and welcoming staff on reception, immaculately clean throughout and extremely reasonable prices (60 euros a night for a single plus another 7 for breakfast).I'm not suggesting that it's faultless - the rooms we stayed in weren't the biggest ever (although I thought they were perfectly adequate for a short stay and let's face it, who wants to go to a city like Madrid and stay in their hotel room?) and I can imagine that some guests who are on the larger side might find it a bit of a squeeze getting into the (fantasically powerful) shower I had in my room. The breakfast was good rather than historic but there was plently of it, with a wide choice of the usual cold meats and cheeses, yogurts, pastries etc plus hot items like scrambled egg, bacon and sausage and good coffee so I'd say it represented value for money. As far as the question of noise which some others have commented on I can only speak for myself and I thought it was one of the quietest hotels I've stayed in with no noticable street noise despite the location (once I remembered to close the window!). Yes, the cleaning staff come around doing the rooms at about 9.00 am but I wouldn't describe them as noisy or disruptive.Just a word on two of the restaurant recommendations we were given by the lovely female receptionist on our first morning. We visited La Gloria de Montera on the Calle Caballero de Gracia and Bazaar on the Calle de la Libertad (I think they're part of the same chain and we found both to be absolutely first-rate with very tasty modern (but unpretentious) dishes, great staff and a brilliant atmosphere. Both places get full early, mainly with locals, and you can't reserve so I'd suggest getting there early..... you won't regret it!Overall we all agreed that the Hotel Plaza Mayor was probably one of the best places we'd stayed at during our regular trips abroad - personally I'd say that the standard was higher than than in many 3* and even 4* hotels I've been to, it's amazingly good value and I'd go back and stay there again without hesitation.

<Author>clyde-valley
<Content>Perfect Location We arrived at the hotel on 3 April and stayed for 4 nights. Check in was quick and straight forward and the staff were helpful and friendly (their English was better than my Spanish).We booked the rooftop 'Suite Del Palomar' which had great views over the city and was very quiet.The inside of the hotel was modern and in good condition and the housekeeping staff cleaned our room each day, changed the towels and left fresh toiletries. As it was very cold and wet during our stay we opted for breakfast a few times. The buffet was pretty good value with a choice of cold meats, tortilla, pastries, fruit cerial, bread and coffee. The hotel couldn't be better placed for visiting the main attractions around the city centre. The Plaza Mayor was about 50 yards away and the 3 main museums around a 10-15 minute leisurely walk. Puerto del Sol was less than a 5 minute walk and a further 5 minutes to Gran Via and onto Malasana and Chueca.Some other reviewers have criticised the hotel, but taking into account the location, the price and the helful staff (and it is only 2 star) I don't think it would be possible to get better value for money. Unless your looking for luxury, I would thoroughly recommend staying here for a city break.

<Author>GPoole
<Content>A Wonderful Hotel My friend and I just returned from a week long visit to Madrid, and stayed for our first time at the Hotel Plaza Mayor. Contrary to the former two reviews, the Hotel Plaza Mayor was wonderful!! Upon arriving, we were greeted by the very friendly and helpful staff. In fact, during our entire stay the receptionists were a fount of information, giving us restaurant and sightseeing tips, as well as having a good command of the English language, since neither of us speak Spanish.Allowing us to have an early check in, we found our room, and were pleasantly surprised at it's size. We have stayed in hotels in Europe, where the rooms were of much smaller size than here. We had an inside room, with a door to a small courtyard, which was extremely quiet. The only noise we ever heard was the charming ringing of a church bell nearby. The room itself was immaculate, lovely wooden floors, and a large and spotless bathroom. Another positive was the price of the room, which we received for about 90 Euros per night, a great bargain in a city that is becoming more and more expensive.I believe the visitor to Madrid would be hard pressed to find a hotel more convenient that the Hotel Plaza Mayor. It is located on the lovely Plaza de Santa Cruz, and so close to the Plaza Mayor that the statue of Philip III is within a few meters. It is a short 15 minutes walk to the Royal Palace and the Prado, and the famous Rastro market is around the corner. The Metro is nearby, and taxicabs are plentiful.A write once wrote that a traveler should always assume that he will return. I will return to Madrid someday, and will not hestitate to stay at this charming hotel. It is highly recommended.

<Author>nysingle
<Content>Pluses outweigh minuses, amazing location The Hotel Plaza Mayor is a great value in an amazing touristy location.It is a half-block away from Plaza Mayor, 5 minutes or so from Sol, and walk-able to everywhere (from Palacio Real to Prado / Sofia), easily accessible from the airport. I stayed there in Jan. 07 for 60 euro a night, a good bargain imho. There are lots of places to eat nearby, I esp. liked a bakery on C. Mayor (La Mallorquina) and a chain restaurant called Cerveceria 100 Montaditos (near Sol, also on C. Mayor).In response to other reviewers. I was able to check in early (off season). I didn't have any problems with the heat, it was perfect. I didn't have any problems with the lighting, but I can see why someone would complain. Noise, as mentioned by others, can be a problem. If it's really loud outside, you can be bothered, but the street noises weren't that bad to me. In some rooms (like mine), the pipes can be very loud, i.e. you can be startled by your neighbor turning on their sink. The room was small, but still a bargain given the location / price, I think.The hotel staff was super, as were their email responses. There's a vending machine (a big plus to me) in the lobby as well as internet access for a small fee. There are several groceries nearby, and a supermarket near Sol in Corte Ingles (basement) and a real market down near Plaza d'Villa (on Mayor).All in all, a great bargain. May not be the place for a special occasion (i.e. honeymoon). The pluses outweigh the minuses.Oh, their contact info is info@h-plazamayor.com.

It is a relatively small hotel but it was a wonderful place to stay due to its very friendly and helpful staff and its fantastic location which is minutes walk from some of Madrid鈥檚 principal attractions.Although the rooms are small, they are very comfortable and the shower is one of the most powerful I've ever come across. My only complaint is that the cleaners start cleaning rooms quite early and they can be noisy, as each of them has a loud walkie-talkie.I had the 鈥榩leasure鈥?of being in the New Years Eve Madrid 10km run鈥?with 20,000 other people. Having done a number of big events including the Great North Run I can tell you that this is a fantastic run to enter. It begins from the Bernabau Stadium at 6pm and goes past every key building and monument. And allows one to see all the city鈥檚 xmas decorations which are beautiful and stretch throughout Madrid. The local support for the runners was amazing all the way along..The Plaza Sol is less than 3 minutes walk from the hotel and it is the centre of the city. New Years eve in the plaza will never be forgotten. Lighting and heating were both fine. Also we got a fantastic deal of 280 Euros for 3 nights鈥︹€?try and match that over New Year..I CAN THOROUGHLY RECOMMEND THIS HOTEL

<Author>Anazus
<Content>Great, great, great! I went to Madrid for the tennis in early November with some friends, we chose this hotel because it was close to the stadium and the reviews here were really good. I was there from Wednesday to Sunday. I booked a single room online with 2 months advance whilst we organized the meeting up and everything was as planned. When I arrived they gave me a double room and asked me to move to a single the next morning, which I did without a problem. The double was a 1st floor room with a huge window to the main street. It wasn't a problem for me but for those who are noise-sensitive, you may prefer a room located on the back as it was the single room I had for the other 3 nights. Both rooms were imaculated clean, the bed was nice, the bathrooms both had great showers, just all I needed!I can't say good enough of the staff! There was a little problem with our tickets for the tennis and one of my friends (who also stayed at the hotel) asked them if they could pick up the tickets at the stadium for us, which they kindly did without charging us any extra fee. <Author>Dasc
<Content>Wouldn't Stay Here Again We stayed at this hotel for two nights. It was the last hotel of our trip and it was the worst. We researched all our hotels on TripAdvisor and this was the only major disappointment. Perhaps the low cost of the room (in a major city) should have been a give-away. We reserved a superior twin room. It's hard to believe that the room was a superior room.... I wonder what a standard room looks like. The room was drab, the lighting was poor (although there were several light fixtures), the furniture looked cheap, and the view was into a narrow, dark courtyard with other windows 10 - 15 feet away. The walls were paper thin. I did pass by a couple of rooms that were being cleaned that looked much nicer. These were painted white, had bright covers on the beds, and looked airy. They had large windows that faced the street. I'm sure I would have had a different opinion of the hotel had we had one of these rooms. On the plus side, the room we had was clean and the bathroom was fine. The hotel staff were friendly and helpful. A male receptionist recommended a very good, reasonably priced restaurant that served non-traditional Spanish food. (By the time we arrived in Madrid, we were ready for something different to eat.) We loved the restaurant. It's called Finca de Susana. It's a good-looking restaurant with white table cloths, reasonable prices and Madrilenos as customers (English menus are available.) The food is eclectic. It was a fairly short walk from the hotel.

<Author>Grnwayrob
<Content>Very Average Madrid Hotel We stayed at the Hotel Plaza Mayor for 4 nights in September. I was really looking forward to our stay from all the positive reviews on this site. We had booked a superior room, paying 10 euro extra believing we would have a larger room. I had also e-mailed the hotel directly and asked for a room with a view in the hopes of getting a room like those pictured with lots of windows. The room we received was nothing like those described here. It was very small, on the first floor ( second floor to Americans), and had one window with a view of the brick wall across the street. The two twin beds were pushed up against the walls with about 2 feet of space between them. There was a modular nightstand in between the beds, so they could not be pushed together as is standard in most European hotels. We did not ask to change rooms as we were tired from travelling all day and had unpacked when it settled in on how small our quarters were. On the bright side, the bathroom was sufficient in size, and the shower had excellent water pressure and plenty of hot water. The room was cleaned daily, and was spotless. We took the buffet breakfast one morning and it was quite filling and tasty. The desk staff though seemed quite bored with their jobs, and were not really friendly. Also it should be noted that although the hotel uses electronic key cards, they are attached to a huge metal weight, so you must leave your key at the front desk when leaving the hotel. Overall, I can't say I would stay here again. There are plenty of alternative hotels and hostals in the neighborhood that offer the same size rooms for half the price. And for 10~20 Euro more a night you can have a nice hotel.  
<Date>Sep 26, 2006

<Author>HCH15
<Content>Plaza Mayor was a good deal and location! My husband and I stayed at this hotel for 3 nights in August - We had a very nice stay and recommend it to others looking for a clean hotel, nice bathroom, and good location for sightseeing!We arrived at Barajas airport and took the metro to the Sol Station (3 changes  45 mins) for a couple of euros. Then we walked to the hotel by going through the actual Plaza Mayor diagonally and found our hotel on a corner. We had easy access to all of the museums by 10-15 min walk on foot and found plenty of food close by. Best of the trip was finding Retiro Park 10 min from the hotel on foot and spending the day on a boat relaxing. Also, the Atocha train station was 15 min on foot, so we took a high speed train to Toledo as a side trip.The hotel itself was clean and staff were friendly. They are on duty 24 hrs/day and buzz you in after dark. The hotel is quaint, with some charm. We didn鈥檛 realize there was an elevator initially but there is one and it helps when you are on the 4th floor. Our room was extremely clean and equipped with the essentials 鈥?Beds were firm, as was to be expected. Air conditioning worked very well. The bedroom was plain, but the bathroom was updated, modern, and very clean! The towels were always fresh and were big. We were pleased that the water was hot and the water pressure could be set anywhere from low to peel off skin high. Breakfast isn't included but you could purchase the buffet in the lobby for 8 euros if you were hungry; otherwise, there were cheap coffee/pastry alternatives within 5 mins of the hotel.

<Author>KilgoreTrout
<Content>A Great Find I found this hotel in a New York Times article about travelling in Europe on a budget. Housed in a beautiful old house, this hotel has been magnificently renovated with all the modern conveniences. The rooms were spotless, featured new beds, furniture and bedding, laminate flooring and large well appointed bathrooms. The AC worked great - which was a blessing considering the 35+ degree heat and the fact I had just spent a week in London where air conditioning seems not to have been invented yet. The walls were thin enough to hear movement in the hallways, but I never heard noise from other rooms, nor was there any noise from the street. Another nice touch was the complimentary postcards which featured a photo of the hotel building taken at the turn of the 20th century. The staff was friendly (all spoke english too), the snack and drink machine in the lobby was handy and the over-priced internet was useful (walk a few blocks to puerta del sol and you can find any number of internet cafes that charge half as much). For 50 euros a night for a double room (albeit during the hotel's low august season) this hotel was a steal. Im surprised after being featured in the new york times it wasnt booked solid. Moreover, the location is perfect, the Plaza Mayor right outside the door, and within walking distance (about two blocks) to Puerta del Sol, the centre of Madrid. I'd definately stay here again.

<Author>Londoner70
<Content>Ideal Location Stayed at the hotle for 2 nights as part of a larger tour of Spain. The location was absolutely perfect. You are just away from the corner of the Plaza Mayor and within walking distance (when not in mid summer heat!) of most major attractions within Madrid. The rooms are basic but clean - but to be honest you won't spend much time in your room. We did not have breakfast here which is extra as there are plenty of places serving very good breakfasts all around the hotel. There are vending machines in the Hotel lobby which provide 24 hour access to snacks and bottled water which is very handy.On a night out you do not need to go on the metro as most restaurants and bars/clubs are within 10 mins walk away. There is security on 24 hours so you just need to press a buzzer to get back in. We would definitely stay here again if we go back to Madrid.

<Author>melbguy
<Content>great value This is small, beautiful hotel in a perfect location at a very reasonable price. The rooms are smallish but beautifully decorated and absolutely spotless. They have individual air conditioning, in-room safes, and marble bathrooms. We were on the fifth floor with a great view and the double-glazed windows kept it quiet. The staff are very friendly and speak excellent English, and the breakfast buffet is surprisingly varied and good value for money. Of course, this is not a five-star hotel and it doesn't have some amenities you might be used to from North American hotels, e.g., no ironing board  iron in the room (a small one can be borrowed), no in-room internet access, few coat hangers, no refrigerator, and the towels aren't exactly soft and plush. Still, an excellent choice for a vacation in central Madrid!

<Content>Plaza Mayor Hotel, Great value! We would only be in Madrid for two nights, so wanted a hotel close to Plaza Mayor as a base for easy walking between sights.Impressed by all the reviews, even ones complaining about small bedrooms or no view etc.By looking at candid photos and emailing hotel several times found out that rooms ending in 03 are on the corner of Hotel over the front door, with a good view over Plaza Santa Cruz.Requested one of these rooms and checked into 503, nice and high. <Author>benthespaniel
<Content>A really great place to stay in Madrid Just back from Madrid. A beautiful city and this is a great place to stay when you're there. Really central location - loads to see and do nearby and plenty places to eat and drink.We were there on the public holidays of 1st and 2nd May so there was no traffic around the hotels on those days but it wasn't a problem.The hotel was very clean, the staff helpful, knowledgeable and friendly. Breakfast buffet looked nice although we didn't eat there, choosing one of the many alternatives nearby for a bit of variety.We stayed in a superior room at the very reasonable rate of 90 Euros a night (Room 203) right above the front door of the hotel. No problems with noise except for me snoring!If you're looking for a luxury hotel to stay inside in in Madrid, this is a poor choice. If you want a great central location for a hotel to have a shower and a sleep before seeing the city, you will struggle to find better.We booked direct with the hotel by phone as the website at --- didn't show availability - but it was there!A few tips on Madrid.....Don't use taxis - use the metro - a taxi to the hotel from the airport cost us 30 Euros. With a bit more confidence we took the metro for a Euro each!Take the Madrid Vision bus tour - 2 days is really good value at 19 euros each - once you have your bearings, then the city is east to explore on foot or by combination of bus and metro.

<Author>Bryyan55
<Content>Good but small As a Christmas present our children sent us to Madrid, Spain for a long weekend break at the end of April 2006. We stayed at the Hotel Plaza Mayor which was ideally located in the centre of Madrid, just outside the famous Plaza Mayor itself.The hotel was very clean and the staff were both friendly and always helpful. The breakfast buffet was good with a wide choice food, cereals, meat, cheeses and fruit etc with a cooked breakfast of scrambled eggs and bacon also being available.Our standard hotel double room 108 on the first floor was clean but extremely small with no chair, one bedside cabinet and a single wardrobe. The comfortable bed was a three quarter size bed and the pillows were very small.The shower room was also modern, very clean but again small.The air conditioning unit did not seem to be very effective even on its lowest setting, how it would perform on a really hot day I am not sure. We had to leave the window open when the temperature was only 24 degrees.It was very difficult to tell whether or not it was daytime or nightime as the window faced a wall and it was hard to see any sky, the room lights always had to be switched on.The cost of this doulble room was 79 euros per night.We did look into other rooms which were much bigger and some were very spacious but none were available as it was the bank holiday weekend. When booking a room at the Hotel Plaza Mayor make sure you ask about the room size, the air conditioning unit and the view from the window.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Our room was good but others were not equal We were happy with our stay at the Hotel Plaza Mayor. We selected it based on other good internet reviews and were not disappointed. We got exactly what we wanted here, clean, good location and moderate price. We did not want to pay extra for luxury like big screen TV, swimming pools, granite, marble and fluff. If you want a resort look elsewhere but if you want to sight see until you drop and have a decent place at decent price stay here. The location is very good in the heart of old town. It is within walking distance of the Sol station subway, shopping, tourist bus, Cava Baja and many interesting sights. We enjoyed 3 large floor to ceiling windows two of which offered a great view of the interesting streets below. Front desk staff spoke great english and were very friendly and positive. Note that the rooms vary significantly, we saw some that were very small with no view and we heard of others that were great. Small but clean and presentable lobby with small restaurant we never tried because there are so many other choices near by. The tour bus Madrid Vision was a good way to see the city, the subway was easy to figure out, the train to Toledo was a good day trip experience. Watch your wallet, a guy tried to pickpocket me on the subway. Hit the Tapas bars in on Cava Baja, soak up some music, you really feel like you are in Spain here.

<Content>Great place and fantastic friendly staff I am not the sort of person who likes being fussed over,and generally like the impersonality of larger establishments. <Author>Miner1
<Content>Only one criticism I stayed in a single room for two weeks while on a course, and agree with other posts that this is a good, central hotel in an excellent position, with very pleasant and helpful staff. The single rooms are quite small, although comfortable enough and clean(I had just enough space to work on my laptop). For the price it is really excellent value. I would make only one criticism. The water is very hot, the shower cubicle is very small. It is very easy to knock the hot water to maximum. The water is then scalding hot - there is nowhere to go: you have to reach through the water for the tap or to get out! OK when you know the problem, but I don't think it would pass the health and safety test in the UK. This may only apply to the single rooms though. There is no restaurant, but the breakfasts are good, no fresh fruit juice being my only complaint, and you can always go across the square for a change.I would certainly book here again.

<Content>Utterly disappointed, unimaginable customer service My wife and I went to Madrid for a 4-day vacation last week and had booked Hotel Plaza Mayor over the internet after reading the reviews here and a couple of other sites. We had given our credit card details and everything over email. The hotel room was great infact. It was a corner room with three windows facing three different streets. Of course, we were hardly in the room to enjoy the view since we left early and returned late.The problem was that on the third day while we were away, they checked us out. We went out in the morning after having breakfast in the hotel and handing over the keys to the front desk. When we came back at 8pm in the night, the front desk tells us that we were checked out since we hadn't given the checkout date and the hotel was booked completely. Now, I do remember that we had requested for only 2 days over email initially but when we actually checked-in we had told them that we will stay for 4 nights since we didn't plan to go to another city. And now they told us that all of our stuff had been moved out of the room. They had even opened the safe and removed the wallet, purse and laptop from there. What more? They opened our bags to keep the other stuff on the table and bathroom inside the bags. I simply cannot understand how can a hotel check someone out like this? We gave the keys in the morning before starting to eat breakfast. Nobody said anything. They had our credit card. We had our stuff in the room, so they could definitely not assume that we will not pay for that night.Stay away from the hotel. After ensuring that nothing was missing from the luggage, my wife and I had to lug around the stuff in a light drizzle to find a hotel. Highly disappointed and would never stay there inspite of the fact that the location is good and the room was quite nice.

<Author>Cobi00
<Content>Excellent Choice for Madrid Tourist We chose this hotel from the previous Tripadvisor reviews, and the reviews were right on target. It was the only budget hotel that did not have any negative Tripadvisor reviews. What we found is that this hotel is a real gem and great value for the money. I travel a lot for business and generally stay in 4 or 5 star hotels. When traveling with my family to Europe using multiple rooms, we try to find a lower cost hotel. I would match this hotel up with any 4-star hotel for most amenities.The hotel is immaculately clean, the service from the English-speaking front desk is top-shelf, and the location is ideal for touring Madrid. The hotel is very quiet even though it is within 100 yards of the Plaza Mayor, the center of Old Madrid. Special thanks to Anucha at the front desk for all of her concierge advice! Some tips...1-The Metro is only 400 meters away (Sol station), safe, very clean and easy to use. Most of the major tourist sites are within 3 kilometers of the hotel. For anything not walkable, I'd recommend using the Metro except for the airport. To or from airport, you can get a taxi for $21-25. 2-We did not eat at the hotel due to the large number of good, inexpensive alternatives within 2 blocks in any direction. However, the hotel buffet looked very good.3-The standard double rooms are quite small. We took 2 superior doubles for our family of four and found them to be fine for size.This was our first visit to Madrid and we loved it. We found it to be very sophisticated, cultured, active, clean and safe. Also, reasonable cost compared to other major cities in Europe. We feel lucky to have found this hotel and will stay there again on our next trip to Madrid, whether for business or pleasure.

<Author>ChristopherPrusaski
<Content>8 Nights in the Attic Suite We just returned from an eight night stay in the Attic suite (the official name is the Palomar Suite, or Room 600). This room is unique to the hotel and definitely the largest room at the Plaza Mayor. We reserved it based solely upon the positive reviews on this site (and thanks to the Australian couple who corresponded with us a few months ago to follow up on their review). All in all, we were not disappointed.HOTEL LOCATION: The front of the hotel is located on one corner of the Plaza Mayor, which is indeed one of the best locations for tourism in the city. Between the front door and the P.M. is a pedestrian plaza with many shops (Plaza Santa Cruz). There are also drug stores and bodegas that sell pretty much anything you might need in the hotel (beer, wine, water, etc.) within a minute's walk. Additionally, the Sol, Opera, and Tirso de Molina Metro stops are all short walks from the hotel (Sol being the closest, about 6-7 minutes, and linking to many lines). Like most all of Madrid, this location is extremely safe and welcoming.THE ROOM: Ok. Not to brag, but we stayed in the Suite, so we can't comment on the other rooms in the hotel (whcih comprise the significant majority of the accommodations). But I will share our experience with you in case you want to try to snag this room yourself.Firstly, in case you're wondering, we only paid 110 EU per night for this room, whcih, in connection with its size, was a fantastic bargain.The Suite is an approx. 450 square foot L-shaped attic room, with slanted ceilings, exposed wood beams (lovely), and three skylight windows (which open). The room is accessable from a private stairway on the fifth floor, next to the elevator. The room has a central A/C and heater unit (the heater worked quite well for us, as it was around 3 C. most nights in Madrid). There is no bathtub, but the shower worked excellently and the bathroom was designed in a pretty modern style. A large cable television, small 'fridge, and a sitting area with two comfy chairs and a living room table made the place special. All in all, a big room.The room also has a large private balcony with wooden chaise lounge chairs and a table with a pretty nice view toward the Plaza Mayor (the mountains surrounding Madrid are also within view). And a nice place to hang your smoky clothes to air out at night (welcome to Spain!).Not only did we not hear any noise at night from other guests (the room is the only room at the top of the hotel) or traffic, the curtains on the numerous windows (and blinds on the skylight windows) would allow us to completely black-out the room to sleep late in the morning. Nice touch and convenient for the Madrid nightlife.HOTEL STAFF: Charming and helpful in all respects. The woman who worked the front desk during the day (I wish I got her name) was a total sweetheart. We kept commenting every day on how nice she was to us. She would greet us each morning with a huge smile and say BUENOS DIAS!, which, being Americans, freaked us out at first, but we eventually shed our inhibitions and learned to well in the sugary sweetness of this sincere hospitality. (And kudos to the young man who worked the midnight shift was also real nice). BREAKFAST: For 6 Euro, pretty good selection of coffee, juices, pastries, eggs, and meats. Charming restaurants are located all over the place, though, in case you want to venture out.WIFI: Located in the lobby and works great and is free.

<Author>WStradlater
<Content>Location, location, location...... A lot is said about location but this hotel had the best of any I stayed in Europe. Superbly positioned spitting distance from Plaza Mayor and roughly halfway between the East-West poles of Madrid's major tourist nodes (Prado and Palace Royal) - the location is truly outstanding. I had room tres, cero, uno (301) which was sensational value at 55 Euros (Double single use). The room itself was smallish but clean with a decent bathroom. It over-looked the Calle Atocha and the view wasn't half-bad - seemed to be opposite some swanky offices. Noise wasn't a problem. The hotel staff were friendly and helpful with good English. I didn't eat breakfast in the hotel so can't comment but there are a million places close-by for fuel replenishment. I had a great evening meal at nearby Los Galayos. If I were back in Madrid I wouldn't think twice about booking this hotel again. A tip for some - if you are doing any day trips out of Madrid the hotel staff will suggest Pulmantur Company. I did the Escorial/Valle de los Caidos half-day tour and the Toledo full day. The Toledo tour I thought was great taking you to some of the less frequented places with some great El-Greco. However, I was dissapointed with the Escorial tour as it is quite rushed and misses out on some of the major rooms. They also offer a full day tour of Avila/Segovia which looked interesting. With 3 day trips and at least 2 days of internal sight-seeing, Madrid can be worth up to a 5-day visit.

<Author>bakio
<Content>Good hotel, super location Stayed here for five nights with my wife and two small children for the Cycling World Championships in September, 2005. Location can't be beat; we walked to everything--big 3 museums, Puerto Del Sol, Palacio Real, Plaza de Oriente (good playground for kids), terrific restaurants on and around Cava Baja, and of course the Plaza Mayor. Bus stop immediately in front of hotel, plus short walk to Sol or La Latina Metro stations gets you anywhere else. Hotel is clean and well-maintained. Our triple room room was small, but who cares when you are in Madrid--you are never in your room anyway! We ate breakfast at the hotel on two mornings. Good selection of breads, cereals, eggs, juices, coffee, and tea. The other mornings we hit the friendly cafeterias between the hotel and the Puerto Del Sol for churros. Hotel staff is very friendly and helpful. For example, they helped us buy tickets for an Atletico soccer game and they gladly made restaurant reservations for us. Will definitely return to Hotel Plaza Mayor and the always-wonderful city of Madrid.

<Author>pepys
<Content>When staff can make a difference.... The Plaza Mayor Hotel is just like a dorm room in college. Same desk, same beds. That said, the entire place is cheerful in lively colors and it is as spotless as any place we have ever stayed. It is so cheap it is a steal and the location by the plaza is superb. It is clean, comfortable, well sited with a very good bathroom. While you may not get spectacular views, Frette sheets, fancy breakfasts (we didn't try it, we never do in hotels as a rule except in Italy) or Carlos V furniture, you do get a terrific deal along with the hotel's secret weapon: an unbelievably friendly, multilingual front desk staff that knows the area and the restaurants and night life. Did I mention they are friendly? Can't overemphasize this enough. Not lux, but delightful for the price.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hit (mostly) or miss (somewhat)... My wife and I and extended family stayed at the PM for two nights this past June, and our experiences as far as the rooms go were quite different. Our room was top-notch and had a wonderful view of the city (it was our second anniversary so we splurged a bit), but my parents' room was barely big enough to fit the bed and had a lovely view of a wall. I would recommend asking for a superior double or whatever they call it if size is in any way important to you, and/or asking to see the room first. That said, the rooms/beds were all clean and comfortable, the bathrooms were a good size, and the location of the hotel is terrific--one block off the Plaza and a straight shot from the train station if you happen to be driving or taking a taxi (right up C/ Atocha.) The front desk staff was also very courteous and helpful. Ask for recommendations to dinner--they know the town well.All in all a good stay for us, the small rooms (in some cases) notwithstanding. Not sure if my parents would agree, however.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice little hotel I stayed at the Plaza Mayor for one night in April after beachfront accomodations in Marbella. It is very convenient for those arriving into madrid from the Atocha train station. The hotel is about ten minutes away by taxi. The Sol metro stop is a block away and was an easy ride to the airport, even with luggage.It is definitely convenient to the party and restaurant district nearby. We arrived around 6 pm so we didn't stray to far to see the other attractions such as the Palace which is not very far. The hotel staff was extremely friendly. Our room was definitely postage stamp size. i was told that we would have a double bed, but that was a stretch, more like a small version of an American full size bed. But as a seasoned european traveler, this posed no problem, just tight sleeping (and living) quarters for two people. After going to bed at 300AM, we definitely could hear other guests as they went to their rooms. At one point, we could feel the movements of the guests in the room next door as they prepared for bed. Thank God, they decided not to partake of one another because it would have definitely have been an up close and personal experience. :-)For a short stay at a no frills, clean and friendly in-town hotel, go for it. If you will be visiting for several nights, and space and insulation from sounds, is more up your alley, then this may not be your place. We woke up to a quartet of Spanish young ladies ending their partying at 6:30AM. You gotta love Spain, I sure did! At 65 euros, I would definitely stay at the Plaza Mayor again. Ciao!

<Author>ramchalice
<Content>Good Location  I recently stayed for three nights at the Hotel Plaza Mayor based on previous reviews. My evaluation is not quite as enthusiastic as most have been. True, the location is extremely convienient, the hotel is clean and the price is very reasonable. However, on the downside, I found the room to be as Spartanly-furnished as any hotel room, even a budget one, as I've ever seen. But most troublesome was the noise factor. The hallways and rooms are not carpeted, the walls are very thin, and the keys and locks are very noisy and must be used to both open and relock the door. Therefore, whenever anyone arrives and departs on your floor you are likely to be awakened. Given the party nature of Madrid, this was every night for me, often at 3:00 and 4:00 a.m. As mentioned in previous reviews, the buffet breakfast is very much to be skipped. Staff were friendly. Not a terrible choice, but I'd probably look elsewhere for my next stay in Madrid.
